    PREFACE

The C─Бrudatta attributed to Bh─Бsa is of perennial interest to the student of Sanskrit literature, as it has given rise to the tantalising problem as to whether it is the original of the Mс╣Ыcchakaс╣нika, or an abridgment thereof. It is probable that there is a third alternative to the problem viz: the possibility that the C─Бrudatta is an abridgment of the play ‘Daridra-C─Бrudatta’ which is referred to as a R┼лpaka by many rhetoricians, and the relation between these three plays will be a matter for further research. We have proceeded on the assumption that ‘Daridra-C─Бrudatta’ is but an alternative title of the Mс╣Ыcchakaс╣нika for reasons given in the introduction. In any case there could be no reasonable doubt that if such a play as the ‘Daridra-C─Бrudatta’ has an independent existence, yet there must be a very close, and in fact, a genetic relation between all the three plays.

The present edition is based upon Gaс╣Зapati ┼Ъ─Бstri’s edition, with occasional references to Morgenstierne’s text as given in his “├Ьber das Verh├дltnis Zwischen C─Бrudatta und Mс╣Ыcchakaс╣нika”. I have made use of Gaс╣Зapati ┼Ъ─Бstri’s commentary in translating and annotating, and have further referred to Woolner’s translation. I here make my grateful acknowledgments to all these writers.

I take this opportunity of expressing my gratitude to Dr. N. G. Sardesai, who has undertaken to bring out this publication and lastly my thanks are due to Mr. S. R. Sardesai, B.A., LL.B., the manager of the Samartha Bharat Press, for the very nice printing and get-up of the work.

Prabh─Бkara Niketana,

Deccan Gymkhana, Poona 4.
C.R. DEVADHAR

29 June 1939.

6. Cheс╣нa a servant to Vasantasen─Б.

Female : -
1. Ganik─Б The Courtesan Vasantasen─Б.
2. Br─Бhmaс╣З─л Wife of C─Бrudatta.
3. Radanik─Б A maid-servant of C─Бrudatta.
4. Madanik─Б A maid-servant and confidante of Vasantasen─Б.
5. Vicchittik─Б… Maids in Vasantasen─Б’s house.
6. Caturik─Б Maids in Vasantasen─Б’s house.
Besides these, there are the usual stage-manager and his wife, the actress.

ITRODUCTION

The C─Бrudatta presents a very interesting problem to the student of literature. As I have remarked elsewhere* it stands apart from the group and has peculiarities which are not shared by the rest of the plays-such as the absence of the introductory verse, of the Bharatav─Бkya and the comparative prolixity of the prologue, in which again, contrary to usual practice the S┼лtradh─Бra speaks Pr─Бkс╣Ыta. There is, moreover, no agreement in regard either to imagery, vocabulary, incidents and devices or dramatic irony, which is to be seen in the remaining plays. Recurrences such as the use of the words рд╕реЛрдкрд╕реНрдиреЗрд╣рддрд╛, ( рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдорд╛, рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реЗрдХ ), рдкрд░рд┐рд╕реНрдкрдиреНрдж ( рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд░рд╛рддреНрд░ ), or of the sentences рдХреЛ рдХрд╛рд▓реЛ ( рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛, рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрдиреж ) or рдЕрд▓рдорд┐рджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рднрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЕрддрд┐рдорд╛рддреНрд░рдВ рд╕рдВрддрдкреНрдп ред ( рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрдиo and рдЕрд╡рд┐рдорд╛рд░рдХ ), рд╕рдмреНрдмрдВ рдЖрдгреЗрджреБ рд╡рдЬреНрдЬрд┐рдЕ рднреЛрдЕрдВрдгрдВ ( рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрди IV. 32 ) are neither numerous, nor peculiar so as to support the idea of common authorship. The stanza рд▓рд┐рдореНрдкрддреАрд╡ рддрдореЛрд╜рдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирд┐etc. which is common to C─Бrudatta and B─Бlacarita is to be met with in the Mс╣Ыcchakaс╣нika also.

The C─Бrudatta is unknown to Sanskrit writers. There are numerous references to a play Daridra-C─Бrudatta, but these are in the first place references to a complete play and not to a fragment or what appears like one, and secondly, they are more likely than not references to the Mс╣Ыcchakatika. The Daridra-C─Бrudatta is cited both in the N─Бс╣нyadarpaс╣Зa and the Abhinavabh─Бrati as a ‘R┼лpaka’ (which is a play comprising between five to ten acts) in the course of a discussion on free will and determination in its relation to the dramatic art. ( рддрддреЛ рджреИрд╡рд╛рдпрддреНрддрдлрд▓реЗ рджрд░рд┐рджреНрд░рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрддрд╛рджрд┐рд░реВрдкрдХреЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп рдЧреМрдгрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреНрдХрдердВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░рдореНрднрд╛рджрдпрдГ рд╕реНрдпреБрдГ ). This clearly refers to a conclusion which is brought about by ‘Destiny’ as in the Mс╣Ыcchakaс╣нika, where C─Бrudatta is saved from the gallows purely through the sudden turn of fortune in his favour when he himself had abandoned all hope of life. Daridra-C─Бrudatta cannot be the present play for the simple reason that in none of the Mss. is it called so, nor in the body of the play is the hero ever described as рджрд░рд┐рджреНрд░рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрддрдГ, but always as рджрд░рд┐рджреНрд░рд╕рд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рд╣рдкреБрддреНрд░рдГ рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрддрдГ. In the Mс╣Ыcchakaс╣нika, however, the expression рджрд░рд┐рджреНрд░рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрдд occurs as many as eight times, and when we remember that our rhetoricians are in the habit of using alternative titles like рд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд╛рдЬрдЪрд░рд┐рддрдореН and рд░рддреНрдирд╛рд╡рд▓реА for рд░рддреНрдирд╛рд╡рд▓реА, we need make no the рджрд░рд┐рджреНрд░рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрдд referred to as a рд░реВрдкрдХ is no other than the рдореГрдЪреНрдЫрдХрдЯрд┐рдХ.

In regard to the relation between the C─Бrudatta and Mс╣Ыcchakaс╣нika, opinion is sharply divided, some believing that the latter is a mere amplified replica of the former, while others hold the opinion that the C─Бrudatta is a mere abridgment of the Mс╣Ыcchaka╚Ыika. As I have thoroughly discussed this question elsewhere, I need only assert here my view that the C─Бrudatta is abridged from the first four acts of the Mс╣Ыcchakaс╣нika, with a few additions and numerous alterations particularly in the verse portions. It gives us 55 verses for 143 verses in the corresponding portion of the Mr. out of which as many as 11 are altogether new. The remaining 44 are common to the two plays, but most of these have lost their smoothness and polish in the altered form in which they are presented in the C─Бrudatta.

The main differences in the two versions may here be enumerated:- The most important of these is the complete absence of the political background which practically permeates the play рдореГрдЪреНрдЫрдХрдЯрд┐рдХ. Thus in the prologue there is a reference to king P─Бlaka ( рдХрджрд╛ рдиреБ рдЦрд▓реБ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдХреБрдкрд┐рддреЗрди рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рдХреЗрди рдирд╡рд╡рдзреВрдХреЗрд╢рдХрд▓рд╛рдкрдорд┐рд╡ рд╕рд╕реБрдЧрдиреНрдзрдВ рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рдкреНрд░реЗрдХреНрд╖рд┐рд╖реНрдпреЗ). In act II Darduraka after his scuffle with M─Бthura, the keeper of the gambling house, refers to the forces of discontent that were rallying round рдЖрд░реНрдпрдХ ( рдХрдерд┐рддрдВ рдЪ рдордо рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╡рдпрд╕реНрдпреЗрди рд╢рд░реНрд╡рд┐рд▓рдХреЗрди рдпрдерд╛ рдХрд┐рд▓

рдЖрд░реНрдпрдХрдирд╛рдорд╛ рдЧреЛрдкрд╛рд▓рджрд╛рд░рдХрдГ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рджреЗрд╢реЗрди рд╕рдорд╛рджрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рднрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд╕реНрдорджреНрд╡рд┐рдзреЛ рдЬрдирдГ рддрдордиреБрд╕рд░рддрд┐ ). In act IV there is the proclamation that king P─Бlaka, disturbed by the seer’s prophesy has arrested ─Аryaka and flung him in a dungeon, whereupon ┼Ъarvilaka, who has just secured Madanik─Б for wife, leaves her to take care of herself and himself proceeds to join his revolutionary comrades. The C─Бrudatta studiously drops all these references.

There is further no mention of C─Бrudatta’s son Rohasena. In the Mr. the child is spoken of as having come out of the inner court to enjoy the cool evening breeze and of having dropped into sleep outside; hence the hero asks Vasantasen─Б, whom he mistakes for his maid Radanik─Б, to wrap the child with his mantle and take it inside the house. The C─Бrudatta, however, drops all reference to Rohasena but in so doing, does not succeed in covering up all traces of the abridgment, for it retains the sentence рдкреНрд░рд╡реЗрд╢реНрдпрддрд╛рдВ рдЕрднреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рдореН of the рдореГрдЪреНрдЫрдХрдЯрд┐рдХ where the causal рдкреНрд░рд╡реЗрд╢реНрдпрддрд╛рдВ is all right since the maid is asked to take the child inside the house; while in the C─Бrudatta ai causal becomes meaningless and ungrammatical.

Similarly there is no reference to a suit in the law-court (рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрд░рдгреЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ). The servant of Sak─Бra (the рдЪреЗрдЯof the рдореГрдЪреНрдЫрдХрдЯрд┐рдХ) is not at all mentioned, and last there is a very great change in the conception of the characters, particularly that of the рд╡рд┐рдЯ.

To my mind all these changes are made with a definite purpose. The author of the C─Бruddatta, whosoever he was, wanted to make a pleasing comedy out of the first four acts of the Mс╣Ыcchakatika, and hence has avoided references to the political revolution, to Rohasena, and to the law-suit which is contemplated by the vengeful ┼Ъak─Бra. He has given us a stage-version of the first four acts and has attempted to give it the form of a complete play and not a fragment. Hence whatever was necessary to the subsequent development of the story, such as the law-suit, the servant of ┼Ъakar─Б viz: рд╕реНрдерд╛рд╡рд░рдЪреЗрдЯ who is responsible for the swapping of the bullock-carts, Rohasena whose demand for a golden cart in place of his clay-cart gives Vasantasen─Б a pretext for once more leaving her ornaments in C─Бrudatta’s house, and the political back-ground: all these are meticulously avoided by our author. The remark рдЕрд╡рд╕рд┐рддрдВ рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрддрдореН repre- sents to my mind the real state of affairs. The end of the fourth act ( рдЕрдореГрддрд╛рдЩреНрдХрдГ рдирд╛рдЯрдХрд╛рдЩреНрдХрдГ рд╕рдВрд╡реГрддреНрддрдГ, and рд╣рддрд╛рд╢реЗ рдорд╛ рдЦрд▓реБ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдп ) seems to point to the same conclusion that the author wants to give finality to the play.

With regard to theрддрд┐рдерд┐ scheme which is introduced by our author( рд░рджрдирд┐рдХреЗ, рдЧреГрд╣рд╛рдгреИрддрдВ рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░рдВ рддреНрд╡рдореНред рд╖рд╖реНрдареНрдпрд╛рдВрд╕рдкреНрддрдореНрдпрд╛рдВ рдЪ рдзрд╛рд░рдпред рдЕрд╣рдорд╖реНрдЯрдореНрдпрд╛рдордирдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрд┐рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдорд┐ред ) we feel that confusion is worse confounded; for it necessitates the assumption that the entire action of the story covers but three days; for in the third act, when the, Vid┼лс╣гaka returns home after the concert he is reminded by the maid that it was the eighth day (the same fact is indicated by the verse рдЕрд╕реМ рд╣рд┐ рджрддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛….. рдЕрд╖реНрдЯрдордкрдХреНрд╖рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ ) and hence he was to take charge of the ornaments. Now in the first act the moon is described as rising up at about 9-30 or 10 p.m. which shows that it was ; рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрдкрдХреНрд╖ while in act III the same is described as setting sometime after midnight, which clearly indicates рд╢реБрдХреНрд▓рдкрдХреНрд╖. This leads to the asumption that over a fortnight must have elapsed between the first and third act. But what then would happen to the Tithi Scheme? Vasantasen─Б left her ornaments with C─Бrudatta on рд╖рд╖реНрдареА; they were in the keeping of the maid onрд╖рд╖реНрдареА and рд╕рдкреНрддрдореА and were handed over after midnight on the day рдЕрд╖реНрдЯрдореА to the Vid┼лс╣гaka when he returned from the music concert, and were stolen from him towards dawn by ┼Ъarvilak─Б. This is a very serious inadvertence from which the Mс╣Ыcchakaс╣нika is happily free, although it is not quite clear in regard to its time-sequence.

With regard to the Pr├дkс╣Ыta of the play, we find that Saс╣Гv─Бhaka, who speaks рдорд╛рдЧрдзреА in the рдореГрдЪреНрдЫрдХрдЯрд┐рдХ, speaks the usual рд╢реМрд░рд╕реЗрдиреА here. The ┼Ъak─Бra speaks рдорд╛рдЧрдзреА as in the Mс╣Ыcchakaс╣нika, with his peculiar idiosyncracy of using the palata рд╢ for the sibilant рд╕.

** рдЧрдгрд┐рдХрд╛** тАФ рдЗрдордВ рддрд╕реНрд╕ рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрддрд╕реНрд╕ рджреЗрджреБ рдЕрдпреНрдпреЛред [ рдЗрдордВ рддрд╕реНрдореИ рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрддрд╛рдп рджрджрд╛рддреНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдпрдГред ]

** рдЧрдгрд┐рдХрд╛** тАФ рдЕрд╣рдВ рдЬрд╛рдгрд╛рдорд┐ рддрд╕реНрд╕ рдЧреЗрд╣реЗ рд╕рд╛рд╣рд╕рдВ рдХрд░рд┐рдЕ рдЖрдгреАрджреЛ рдЕрдЕрдВ рдЕрд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реЛред рддрд╕реНрд╕ рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдгрд┐ рдЕрдгреБрдХрдореНрдкреЗрджреБ рдЕрдпреНрдпреЛред [ рдЕрд╣рдВ рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдорд┐ рддрд╕реНрдп рдЧреЗрд╣реЗ рд╕рд╛рд╣рд╕рдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреАрддреЛрд╜рдпрдорд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рддрд╕реНрдп рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдирдиреБрдХрдореНрдкрддрд╛рдорд╛рд░реНрдпрдГред ]

** рд╕рдЬреНрдЬрд▓рдХрдГ** тАФ (рдЖрддреНрдордЧрддрдореН) рдХрдердВ рд╡рд┐рджрд┐рддреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдореНрдпрдирдпрд╛ред

** рдЧрдгрд┐рдХрд╛** тАФ рдХреЛ рдПрддреНрде, рдкрд╡рд╣рдгрдВ рджрд╛рд╡ рдЕрдпреНрдпрд░рд╕ред [ рдХреЛрд╜рддреНрд░, рдкреНрд░рд╡рд╣рдгрдВ рддрд╛рд╡рджрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдпред ]

** рдорджрдирд┐рдХрд╛** тАФ рдгреЗрдорд┐рд╕рджреНрджреЛ рд╡рд┐рдЕ рд╕реБрдгреАрдЕрджрд┐ред рдЖрдЕрджреЗрдг рдкрд╡рд╣рдгреЗрдг рд╣реЛрджрд╡реНрд╡рдВред [ рдиреЗрдорд┐рд╢рдмреНрдж рдЗрд╡ рд╢реНрд░реВрдпрддреЗред рдЖрдЧрддреЗрди рдкреНрд░рд╡рд╣рдгреЗрди рднрд╡рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореНред ]

** рдЧрдгрд┐рдХрд╛**тАФ(рд╕реНрд╡реИрд░рд╛рднрд░рдгреИрд░реНрдорджрдирд┐рдХрд╛рдорд▓рдЩреНрдХреГрддреНрдп) рдЖрд░реБрд╣рджреБ рдЕрдпреНрдпреЛ рдЕрдпреНрдпрд╛рдП рд╕рд╣ рдкрд╡рд╣рдгрдВред [ рдЖрд░реЛрд╣рддреНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдп рдЖрд░реНрдпрдпрд╛ рд╕рд╣ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд╣рдгрдореНред ]

** рдорджрдирд┐рдХрд╛** тАФ рдЕрдЬреНрдЬреБрдП ! рдХрд┐рдВ рдПрджрдВред [ рдЕрдЬреНрдЬреБрдХреЗ ! рдХрд┐рдореЗрддрддреНред ]

** рдЧрдгрд┐рдХрд╛** тАФ рдорд╛рдЦреБ рдорд╛рдЦреБ рдПрд╡рдВ рдордиреНрддрд┐рдЕред рдЕрдпреНрдпрд╛ рдЦреБ рд╕рд┐ рджрд╛рдгрд┐рдВ рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрддрд╛редрдЧрд╣реНрдгрджреБ рдЕрдпреНрдпреЛред (рдорджрдирд┐рдХрд╛рдВ рдЧреГрд╣реАрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рдЬреНрдЬрд▓рдХрд╛рдп рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ред) [ рдорд╛рдЦрд▓реБ рдорд╛рдЦрд▓реНрд╡реЗрд╡рдВ рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ред рдЖрд░реНрдпрд╛ рдЦрд▓реНрд╡рд╕реАрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рд╕рдВрд╡реГрддреНрддрд╛ред рдЧреГрд╣реНрдгрд╛рддреНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдпрдГред ]

** рд╕рдЬреНрдЬрд▓рдХрдГ** тАФ (рдЖрддреНрдордЧрддрдореН) рднреЛрдГ ! рдХрджрд╛ рдЦрд▓реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рднрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ред рдЕрдерд╡рд╛, рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдкрд╛рдкрдореНред

C─АRUDATTA

TRANSLATION

Act I

PROLOGUE

  • (At the end of the Benediction, enter the StageтАФmanager.)*

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФI left my house just at dawn to-day and now my eyes are as it were rolling with hunger like two drops of water on a lotus-leaf! (Walking about) So I will go home and see if there is any arrangement made. (Moving about) This is our house. So I will go in. (Entering and turning round) As the floor has been blackened and variegated by the turning round of ironpots, and there is the scent like the unctious smell of grease when being purified, and here are pious devotees moving about like some auspicious omen, so is it likely that arrangements (of a meal) are ready ? Or that in my hunger the whole world appears to me to be made of rice? I will just call my wife. Madam, will you come here a moment ?

(Entering)

** ACTRESS**тАФHere I am, sir ; it is a good thing you have come.

** STAGE**-MANAGERтАФMadam, is there anything for breakfast in our house?

** ACTRESS**тАФYes, sir.

** STAGE**тАФMANAGER-May you live long! thus may you be (ever) the giver of good food!

** ACTRESS**тАФSir, I have been waiting just for you.

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФWell, dear, is there what I want?

** ACTRESS**тАФYes, sir.

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФSo may the gods bless you! Now what have you got, my dear?

** ACTRESS**тАФThere is ghee, raw sugar, curds and rice.

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФAll this in our house?

** ACTRESS**тАФNo, no, in the market.

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФ(Angrily) Oh, you vile woman, so may your hopes be cut off ! And you shall go to perdition. I am like a sheaf of grass lifted high up from the hill-top by a fierce wind and then let fall again.

** ACTRESS**тАФWell, well, do not be alarmed. Wait a while, sir. Everything will be ready. Why, I have already got it. You will please assist me, sir, in my fast today.

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФWhat is the name of this fast of yours, madam?

** ACTRESS**тАФIt is a fast to get a worthy husband.

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФWhat, in the next life?

** ACTRESS**тАФQuite so.

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФLet all that be. But who has advised you to adopt this fast?

** ACTRESSтАФ**This pious man, C┼лrс╣Зagoс╣гс╣нha.

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФWell done, C┼лrс╣Зagoс╣гс╣нha, well done.

** ACTRESS**тАФIf you will favour me, sir, then I should like to invite some Br─Бhmaс╣Зa worthy of our company.

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФA most pious command. So shall I get a good breakfast too. Well then, you go in, madam, and I, on my part, will find a Br─Бhmaс╣Зa worthy of our company.

** ACTRESS**тАФAs you command, sir.
(Exit)

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФWhere can I find a poor Br─Бhmaс╣Зa? (Looking) Ah, here comes the noble Maitreya, the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa who C─Бrudatta’s friend. So I will invite him. (Moving round) Sir, I invite you. In this matter of invitation, do not despise me on the ground of

my poverty. There will be rich food to eat. There is ghee, raw sugar curds, rice, everything; besides, you will have a gift of gold pieces, too.

(Behind the scenes)

Well, well, invite somebody else. I am not free.

** STAGE-MANAGER**тАФPlease to enjoy, good sir, this rice, well prepared with butter and raw sugar and curds, and served with hot curry and condiments, this exquisite rice offered with great respect. (1)

          (Exit)

End of Prologue.

(Then enter the Vid┼лс╣гaka. )

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФWell, well, invite some one else. I am not free. Well, I say I am not free. What say you? There will be rich food to eat? Well, but I know one would not eat the stone of the very sweetest mango, because that is improper. Now why would you keep on importuning me? I say I am engaged. What say youтАФтАШThere will be a gift of gold coins?тАЩ

Ah, he appears to be repudiated in words (only) but my heart follows him. Oh, misery! That even I should be looking for the invitations of others! I used to pass my days in C─Бrudatta’s house ruminating savoury sweetmeats like a bull at the cross-roads, stuffed up to my very throat, surrounded by a variety of dishes like a painter by numerous pans of paint-dishes that were kept ready throughout the twenty-four hours, seasoned with asafcetida, emitting a sweet fragrance at each breath, commanded by a mere lift of the brow, with numerous drinks thrown in; but the same I, now that the noble C─Бrudatta is poor, must live the life of common people, like the pigeons, moving about else- where for my food and then returning to his house.

And there is another wonderful thing: my belly understands the changed condition. It is satisfied with quite a little; and it will bear a good weight of rice when it is offered. It does not demand what is not offered, nor reject (what is offered). Not that I am not satisfied with such a state of affairs.

Here I have got for the noble C─Бrudatta, who has performed the religious duties (pertaining) to the sixth day these flowers and this upper garment; so I will be by his side. (Stepping around and looking) Here is the noble C─Бrudatta, lovely and yet pitiful like the moon at dawn, stepping this way after worshipping the household deities according to his means, So I will approach him.

(Exit)

(Then enter the Hero offering oblation, the Vid┼лс╣гka, and a maid-servant
with wood-sorrel in her hands.)

HERO, (Sighing deeply)тАФOh, poverty is indeed a living death to a high-minded person; for
On this threshold of my house, where swans and flocks of cranes separated the flowers from oblations, just there have grown the sprouts of corn of old oblations ; and the handful of seeds offered there is eaten by mouths of worms. (2)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФDon’t you, my friend, worry yourself too much. The young days of a house, like those of a man, are subject to changed conditions. Poverty certainly becomes you who have lost your wealth in charity over the entire land upto the sea, as the loss of light becomes the moon of the dark fortnight.

** HERO**тАФNay, I do not bewail my lost fortune. But the ruin of a man who knows the joys of virtue appears to me to be more frightful; for

Happiness after the experience of misery is glorious

like the sight of a lamp in the midst of darkness; but he who comes to poverty after prosperity lives dead with a body alive. (3)

** VID┼кс╣вAKAтАФ**Ah! friend where has it all gone, such hoards of wealth, the choicest from sea and town?

** HERO**тАФ(Sighing)тАФFriend, gone where my fortune is sunk.See,

My wealth is spent in helping my friends; nor do I remember any one that was refused. This my spirit; however, that has paid the price of confidence, does not perish. (4)

(Gesticulates grief.)

** VID┼кс╣вAKAтАФ**Are you grieving for wealth and prosperity?

** HERO**тАФIn truth, I am not brooding over the loss of riches; for it can come again with a turn of fortune; but this is what burns me at heart, that with the loss of the splendour of riches, my friendship towards the good becomes relaxed. (5)

Moreover, if a man be poor his kinsmen will not abide by his words, his magnanimity becomes ridiculous, and the lustre of the moon of character fades away. Without enmity his friends turn away from him and his difficulties multiply; while the evil deeds that others have done are put upon his head. (6)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФThese damnable money transactions are leaving the house like cowherd-boys scared by flies. But the more you brood over the sorrow at loss of wealth, the more will it sprout up like each shoot of an old clump of reeds in spring. So enough of grieving over it.

** HERO**тАФFriend, why should I be grieving? Moreover, am I poor

Whose wife will follow my fortunes, and who have a friend in you that will share my joys and woes?

And what is not found with the poor, I have not lost my magnanimity. (7)

(Enter a courtesan in flurry followed by Viс╣нA and S’ak─Бra.)

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФStop, stop Vasantasen─Б, stop.

Why do you go, run, race away stumbling? Well, be pleased, I won’t slay you. Just stay; my body is now being burnt by love like a bit of leather fallen in the midst of burning cinders. (8)

** VIс╣мA**тАФVasantasen─Б,

Why, with thy grace transformed in fright, thy feet which through instructions in dancing should lightly trip, (now) falling heavily, why dost thou flee like a gazelle frightened by a tiger’s pursuit? Why should thine eyes dart sidelong glances that are tremulous and frightened? (9)

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФOld man, here goes Vasantasen─Б.

Closely followed by us two like a she-jackal by a couple of hounds, with anklets on, and with the (merry) laughter of her tinkling girdle, she has stolen my heart with the pericardium. (10)

** VIс╣мA**тАФVasantasen─Б,

Covering a hundred steps in one step why dost thou glide away like a female snake overwhelmed with the fear of the lord of birds? When I run at full speed, I am like the wind; or can I not indeed, catch thee? (11)

COURTESAN, (Looking around)тАФPallavaka! Pallavaka! Parabhс╣Ыtik─Б! Parabhс╣Ыtik─Б! Madhukarik─Б! Madhukarik─Б! S─Бrik─Б! S─Бrik─Б! Alas, I have lost my servants, so I must protect myself by myself.

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФShout away, lady, shout for the sprout, the cuckoo, the bee, the starling, or for the whole month of spring. Who, indeed, can protect you?

Will it be V─Бsudeva, the lord of the city of the dead,

or Janamejaya, the son of Kunt─л? Seizing thee by the tresses of thy hair, I shall carry thee off as Du┼Ы┼Ы─Бsana did S─лta. (12)

** VIс╣мA**тАФVasantasen─Б, think of me as a man whose heart is entirely innocent of fear. See,

The darkness of night is familiar to me from the vices of my nature. I have already passed through sidealleys darkened by the murk of black nights. Though it should not be declared before a young woman, yet my witnesses are the guards of the market-place who have escaped being murdered. (13)

** COURTESAN**тАФNow I am in doubt of my life, since he vaunts his own qualities. How will such abstain from evil deeds?

** VIс╣мA**тАФLady, do comply with our request. Look you: a request refused generates anger ; and what cannot persons like me do when in anger? You are wooed by this powerful hand of mine made long by the sword. Save me and save yourself from the horror of a young woman’s murder. (14)

** COURTESAN**тАФEven his wooing is frightening.

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФ Vasantasen─Б, the old man speaks well. Surely one should make much of the wooing of a mighty man which is so rare. Look you, girl,

Sharp is the sword, black like a peacock’s neck. I will cut off your head or slay you. Have done with provoking men like us. When a person is dead, he surely lives no more. (15)

** COURTESAN**тАФGood sir, I am but a courtesan who depends for her living on the virtuous satisfaction of the acions of noble families.

** VIс╣мA**тАФSure, that is why we are after you.

** COURTESAN**тАФGood sir, what do you seek from me, my person or my ornaments?

VIс╣мA тАФ A creeper should not be stripped of her flowers. Have done with your ornaments.

COURTESAN тАФ Let me not worry myself now.

** ┼ЪAK─АRA** тАФ Vasantasen─Б, you should make love to me тАФ a prince.

** COURTESAN** тАФ You will rest in peace.

** ┼ЪAK─АRA** тАФ Listen, old man, listen. This Vasantasen─Б asks me to rest in peace.

** VIс╣мA** тАФ

(To himself) The dolt does not see that she is cursing him! When she says тАЬYou will be deadтАЭ he thinks she means тАЬTiredтАЭ. Moreover,

He speaks, gesticulating with all his limbs; and what he says is utterly devoid of sense. His movements are improper, his speech vulgar. Here is a new incarnation of a beast in human form. (16)

(Aloud) Vasantasen─Б, what is it you are saying to my face, so contrary to the ways of courtesans? Look you, The courtesan’s house must be reckoned as the resort of all young men; think of yourself, a courtesan, as a wayside creeper! Your body is like merchandise, to be purchased with money. So serve equally the man you love and the man you hate.) (17)

** COURTESAN** тАФ He tests my liking by my birth.

** ┼ЪAK─АRA** тАФ Old man, here is a lane filled with profound darkness. Don’t let the girl give us the slip down there. Ever since the festival of the Love -God, she has been in love with the poor merchant’s son, the lad C─Бrudatta, pleasing only to the eye. Here is the side-door of his house.

** COURTESAN** (Delighted, to herself) тАФ This is his house. Fortunately the harassment of my enemies brings me close to my beloved. Well, I will do it. (Slips away.)

┼ЪAK─АRA тАФ Eh, old man, the wench is lost, she has slipped away.

** VIс╣мA**тАФHow could she be lost? Search her out, do search her out.

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФOld man, she is nowhere to be seen.

** VIс╣мA**тАФConfound it all, we have been tripped up! Vasantasen─Б, you will soon be found out.

Although you are not to be seen in the evening dusk, like lightning confined in the maw of a cloud, yet the perfume wafted by the breeze and the jingling ornaments will betray you. (18)

(The courtesan removes the garland and
takes away her ornaments.)

** VIс╣мA**тАФAh! how profound is this darkness. For now,

Darkness seems to anoint (my) limbs, and sky to rain down lampblack; while my sight is all profitless to me like service done to a vile person. (19)

Moreover,
As a ready shelter from dangers and also a source thereof, darkness and a dense forest stand equal.For darkness protects bothтАФthe one that causes fear and the other that is troubled by it. (20)

Moreover,
My sight, which could take a wide view in light, being all of a sudden sealed by entering darkness, is as though closed though wide open, owing to the gloom. (21)

** COURTESAN**тАФThe change in the wall (the break in the continuity of the wall) suggests a side-door. And the darkness here is intense as this part (of the house) is not in use. So I shall wait here. (Stands still.)

** HERO**тАФMaitreya, go, and make oblation to the mothers in the square.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФI have no faith. Let someone else go.

** HERO**тАФWhat do you mean?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФMy intellect is like a reflection in a mirror, where right appears left and left, right.

** HERO**тАФIdiot, one must worship according to one’s means Gods are pleased with one’s devotion. So get along.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФHow can I go alone?

** HERO**тАФRadanik─Б, follow this gentleman.

** RADANIK─А**тАФAs my master commands.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФI will take the lamp, lady.

** HERO**тАФLet it be, as you think.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФ(Taking the lamp) Radanik─Б, open the side-door.

** RADANIK─А**тАФVery well. (Gesticulates opening of the door.)

(The courtesan extinguishes the lamp with the skirt of her garment).

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФAlas! Alas!

** HERO**тАФFriend, what is it?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФAs I was going out, a gust of wind from the street came massed up through the open side-door and put out the lamp in my hand.

** HERO**тАФIdiot, fie upon you !

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФIt was only a small mistake. Radanik─Б, go, wait for me in the square. I will join you in a moment with a lamp from the inner room. (Exit.)

** MAID**тАФVery well, sir, (Moves about.)

** COURTESAN**тАФFortunately the door opens to admit me. I should not worry about my virtue. So I will enter.

(Enters and waits.)

** VIс╣мAтАФ**(Observing, to himself) Here is some woman coming out of the house. Good, let me deceive this simpleton with her. (Aloud). Here is perfume that appears to be mingled with the incense of a scented bath.

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФAy, old man, I can hear the smell with my ears, but I can’t see it properly with my nostrils, they are so full of darkness.

** VIс╣мA**тАФStop, stop, where are you going? (Seizes the maid.)

(The maid falls to the ground in fright.)

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФCatch her, old man, catch her.

** VIс╣мA**тАФHere is she, who spurned the scions of noble families in the pride of her youth, being dragged by her tresses that should be adorned with flowers. (22)

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФOld man, have you caught her ?

** VIс╣мA**тАФYes, she is caught by the trail of the scent.

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФNow, I will cut off the head of this slave girl and then kill her.

** VIс╣мA**тАФJust catch hold of her.

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФ(Seising the maid)

Now I have seized this wench, by the head, by the hair, by the tresses, by the locks; now you may coo, or scream or squeal distressingly to the Great Lord, to ┼Ъank─Бra, or to the Almighty. (23)

(Drags the maid with force.)

** MAID**тАФWhat are you about, gentlemen ?

┼ЪAK─АRAтАФOld man, I can tell from her voice that she is not Vasantasen─Б.

** VIс╣мA**тАФDon’t release her. She is Vasantasen─Б, and none else.

Being on the stage, and trained in the arts, surely she is clever at speaking with a changed voice; so do not let her go. (24)

(Entering)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФ(Holding a lamp) Here I come with the lamp, keeping it alight with the greatest difficulty, as at each step the oil in the bowl is shaken up into waves by the cool breeze blowing down the street.

** MAID**тАФ(Kicking S’ak─Бra and crying) O sir, O Maitreya, is this insult or insolence ?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФNone of that, now, none of that. (Stands in suspense at sight of Viс╣нa and S’ak─Бra with swords in hand.)

** VIс╣мA**тАФWhy, this is Maitreya, friend to the noble C─Гrudatta. This, too, is not Vasantasen─Б. Great Brahmin, we acted thus owing to mistaken identity and not through insolence. Look you, sir,

We were after a certain lady, mistress of her youth, who did not love us; she gave us the slip; but through mistaking this lady for her, we have committed this breach of decorum. (25)

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФOh, damn! She happens to be the maid-servant of that fellow C─Бrudatta, the son of a poor merchant, and not Vasantasen─Б. Good, Vasantasen─Б, good. Entering darkness in between you deceived the old man. And I was deceived by the deceitful tricky wench. That is wholly such a nasty business.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФNay, now, this is not right.

** VIс╣мA**тАФOh Great Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, here I fold my hands, which isthe all-in-all of supplication.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФWell, well. It is not your fault. The fault is rather mine that I should let you entreat me.

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФOld man, you seem be mightily afraid of that brat C─Бrudatta, the son of a poor merchant.

** VIс╣мA**тАФTruly, I am afraid of him.

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФWhy, old man, why?

** VIс╣мA**тАФBecause of his virtues. Look you,

He is rendered poor by the suits of men like me ; nor is there any one who is not adorned by his riches. He is like an extensive lake dried up in summer, but dried up after quenching men’s thirst. (26)

Great Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, please do not tell the merchant’s son about this matter.

(Exit Viс╣нa.)

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФM─Бriс╣гa, my lad, sir, speak to the poor merchant’s son, the fellow C─Бrudatta, in my name-the King’s brother-in-law, Saс╣Бsth─Бna salutes you with his turbaned head and says:тАФ the dancing-girl Vasantasen─Б, fair as gold, the daughter of a courtesan, when pursued per force by two of us, has entered your house with a lot of golden ornaments. She must be handed over tomorrow. Otherwise there will be serious trouble between us. My lad, sir, you can also addтАФтАЬLet me not, you son of a slave, break your skull like some bulbous root in the throat of a turtle-dove; let me not crack your head like a ripe wood-apple caught between two doorsтАЭ.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФWell, as you say. (Frightens the S’ak─Бra with the lamp.)

** ┼ЪAK─АRA**тАФ(Looking all round him) Why, where is the old man? He is gone! Alas, the old man !

(Exit S’ak─Бra.)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФLet us tell the noble gentleman that we have made the offering to the deities. Lady, put away resentment from your heart; let not a word be said about this business inside the house.

** MAID**тАФSir, sure I am Radanik─Б.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФCome, let us go. (Both walk about.)

** HERO**тАФMy good girl, is the offering to the deities made?

** COURTESAN**тАФ(To herself) He addresses me as his maid. Never mind, I am saved.

** HERO**тАФThe evening is breezy; so take this mantle.

** COURTESAN**тАФ(Takes the mantle; with joy) The perfume of the mantle suggests that his youth has not yet lost its ardour.

** HERO**тАФRadanik─Б, you had better enter the inner room.

** COURTESAN**тАФ(Aside) I have not the good fortune to enter the inner room.

** HERO**тАФWell, why don’t you enter?

** COURTESAN**тАФWhat am I to say now?

** HERO**тАФWhy do you tarry, Radanik─Б?

(Radanik─Б and Vid┼лс╣гaka advancing)

** MAID**тАФMy master, here I am.

** HERO**тАФWho, then, is this lady?

Contaminated by my garment which in ignorance I offered her, she shines like a digit of the moon covered up by autumn clouds. (27)

** COURTESAN** (Aside)тАФHe is the same person the loveliness of whose form is revealed in the lamp-light, and for whose sake I bear a body kept together only by sighs.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФWell, C─Бrudatta, the king’s brother-in-law, Saс╣Бsth─Бna, salutes you with his turbaned head and saysтАФтАЬThe dancing girl, Vasantasen─Б, the daughter of a courtesan, forcibly carried away by us entered your house with a lot of golden ornaments. She must be handed over tomorrowтАЭ.

** COURTESAN**тАФSo he says тАЬforcibly carried awayтАЭ. Well, then, this is the proper time. (Aloud) Sir, I seek your protection.

** HERO**тАФDon’t be afraid, don’t be afraid. Is this Vasantasen─Б?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФWhat! Vasantasen─Б! (Aside) Oh C─Бrudatta, this is that Vasantasen─Б, who since the festival of the Love-God is acquainted only with your eyes, but is borne by your heart where love is present. So look at her.

** HERO**тАФFriend, I see her,

On whom my love is fixed, when the hoard of my wealth is gone; like the wrath of a coward must it subside in my own breast. (28)

** COURTESAN**тАФI have done wrong by entering the place without invitation; and so with my bent head I beg your pardon.

** HERO**тАФIf that be so, I, too, must beg to be excused for having unwittingly treated you as a servant.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФLike a pair of ill-trained bulls pulling a cart in opposite directions, these two are worrying one another. Now whom may I propitiate? Well, now I will beseech Radanik─Б. Radanik─Б, I beg of you to pardon me.

** HERO**тАФLady, I am your servant. What does love command me to do?

** COURTESAN** (Aside)тАФI should really seek what is sweet. But it would be rather improper to stay here on our first meetingтАФwhen I came here just by chance. So I will do this. (Aloud) If, sir, you are pleased with me, let these my ornaments be left here, for the wicked men pursue me because of my ornaments. And I would like to go home under the protection of the noble gentleman.

** HERO**тАФHer suggestion is quite proper. Maitreya, take (the ornaments).

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФNay, I have no faith.

** HERO**тАФTake them, you fool.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФAs you command. Bring them, lady.

(Courtesan takes off her jewellery and hands it over.)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**, (Taking it)тАФRadanik─Б, take these golden ornaments; and you keep them on the sixth and seventh day. I will keep them on the eighth which is a holiday.

** MAID**тАФ(Laughing) Sure, the young master who is busy with his studies, will find some spare time on that day. Well, bring them, sir. (Takes them and exit.)

** HERO**тАФHo, who is there? Bring a lamp.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФSir, there is no oil in the lamp, as there is no love in a courtesan.

** HERO**тАФWell, there is no need of a lamp. (Observing) Here rises the divine moon, the common lamp of the world. So,

Pale as moist dates, the moon is up to light the royal road, a friend to young women; while through the gloom her white rays descend like streams of milk on dried up mire. (29)

Lady, now you can go on the royal highway. Friend, follow the lady.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФAs you command. Come along, lady, come.

(Exeunt Omnes.)

End of Act 1.

Act II

(Then enter the Courtesan and a Maid.)

** COURTERSAN**тАФWhat next?

** MAIDтАФ**But I said nothing. How do you ask тАЬWhat next ?тАЭ

** COURTESAN**тАФWhat did I say, my dear?

** MAID**тАФMistress, it is love, not officiousness, asks the question. What is in your mind?

** COURTESAN**тАФWhat do you guess, my dear?

** MAID**тАФI guess that owing to absence of the need to pursue a courtesan’s profession, my mistress is in love with some one.

** COURTESAN**тАФYou have guessed rightly. You have an unerring understanding. That is what is really the matter with me.

** MAID**тАФI think my mistress is adorned, though she is without her jewellery. The God of Love is an unexceptional festival of the young.

** COURTESAN**тАФSilly girl, how can you love an object that causes anxious longing ?

** MAID**тАФMistress dear, I want to ask, if he is some prince as lovely as he is respectable.

** COURTESAN**тАФI seek pleasure, not service.

** MAID**тАФCan it be some Brahmin youth fascinating with his deep learning?

** COURTESAN**тАФPerfect confidence is highly cherished. I should have to reverence such a person.

** MAID**тАФIs it a visitor, some merchant’s son?

** COURTESAN**тАФMad girl, what woman in love would bear the blasting of her hopes?

** MAIDтАФ**Can I not hear, then, who is this our brother-in-law- elect?

** COURTESAN**тАФWereyou not present at the Love-God’s festival?

** MAID**тАФYes, I was.

** COURTESAN**тАФThen why talk as if you know nothing?

** MAID**тАФSpeak out, mistress dear, speak out.

** COURTESAN**тАФListen, my dear. It is the merchant’s son C─Бrudatta.

** MAID**тАФWho protected you, when you sought shelter ?

** COURTESAN**тАФThe same.

** MAID**тАФAlas, but he is poor.

** COURTESAN**тАФThat is why I am in love with him. A courtesan in love with a poor man is not reproached.

** MAID**тАФBut, mistress, do the bees settle on a mango when it is past blossoming?

** COURTESAN**тАФYes, my dear, they settle; and that is why they are called (blamed as ) honey-seekers.

** MAID**тАФBut what if owing to loss of wealth he is shy of frequenting a courtesan’s house, and does not come for fear that it would create trouble?

** COURTESAN**тАФBut I love him.

** MAID**тАФIf you have such high regard for him, why don’t you go after him ?

** COURTESAN**тАФNot that I would not go. But if I go to him all of a sudden, and he finds himself unable to return my obligation, I will not be able to see him again; that is why I am tarrying.

** MAID**тАФAh, so that was why you left your ornaments at his place.

** COURTESAN**тАФThat is it.

(Enter a Shampooer, with a hurried toss of the curtain. )

** SHAMPOOER**тАФLady, I throw myself on your protection.

** COURTESAN**тАФCome, do not have any fear.

** MAID**тАФOh, but who is this fellow?

** COURTESAN**тАФMad girl, does one question, a person who seeks shelter?

** MAIDтАФ**But supposing he is some violent fellow?

** COURTESAN**тАФSilly girl, a man of virtue deserves to be protected.

** SHAMPOOER**тАФLady, I forgot my manners through fear, not through impudence. You see, noble lady, those who are frightened, or harried, or overwhelmed, or those of easy virtue, are prone to give offence.

** COURTESAN**тАФWell, well. Be at your ease, sir. I am only a courtesan.

** SHAMPOOER**тАФBy birth only, not by character.

** COURTESAN**тАФMy dear, just so.

** MAID**тАФMistress wants to know from you, sir, what frightened you.

** SHAMPOOER**тАФA creditor, lady.

** COURTESAN**тАФIf it is only that, give the gentleman a seat.

** MAID**тАФVery well. (Offers him a seat. )

** COURTESAN**тАФSit down, sir.

** SHAMPOOER**тАФ(Aside) From this special hospitality, I infer I shall succeed in my object. (Sits down.)

** COURTESAN**тАФMy dear, just this.

** MAID**тАФVery well, my lady. Sir, my mistress desires to make your movements on the royal road free of any embarrassments. What is to be done, and to whom?

** SHAMPOOER**тАФListen, lady.

** COURTESAN**тАФI am all attention.

** SHAMPOOER**тАФP─Бс╣нaliputra is my birth-place. I am a trader by origin. But owing to reverses of fortune I now follow the profession of a shampooer.

** COURTESAN**тАФSo you are a shampooer. You have learnt a delicate art.

** SHAMPOOER**тАФI learnt it as an art. But now it gives me my livelihood.

** COURTESAN**тАФYour words seem to betray bitterness. What then ?

** SHAMPOOERтАФ**Lady, so having heard about it from visitors, and being keen on seeing great men, I came to Ujjayin─л.

** COURTESAN**тАФAnd then?

** SHAMPOOER**тАФImmediately I came to this place, I met a certain merchant’s son.

** COURTESAN**тАФWhat was he like?

** SHAMPOOER**тАФA fine figure of a man, self-possessed, free from conceit, of a gracious presence, but not vain of his graces; clever and sweet, able and (yet) polite, esteemed, not flaunting his virtues, and contented. He gives, but boasts not of it; remembers even the smallestof good turns, and forgets even the greatest of wrongs. My lady, what need to say more? Even a long full day of summer will scarcely suffice to recount a quarter of the virtues of this noble youth. What more, he regards his own person as if it were for the use of others.

** COURTESAN**тАФ(Aside) my good girl, who could this be that emulates the virtues of the noble C─Бrudatta?

** MAID**тАФI too am curious to know. Who could this be that adorns our city of Ujjayin─л with his virtues ?

** COURTESAN**тАФWhat next?

** SHAMPOOER**тАФThen, enslaved by his virtues, I forgot my wife and became his attendant.

** COURTESAN**тАФIs he poor?

** SHAMPOOER**тАФHow could you tell that, lady, without beingtold?

** COURTESANтАФ**It is difficult to find all merits in one place.Well, go on.

** MAID**тАФWho is the gentleman ?

** SHAMPOOER**тАФThe noble C─Бrudatta.

** COURTESAN**тАФThat is right. What more?

** SHAMPOOER**тАФThen on account of his slender means, he dismissed his servants, and relieved of the burden of supporting a household, he is living in the merchant’s house, with nothing left but his good name. I, too, was asked by him to serve another master. But filled withdespair at the thought that I would never find another jewel of a man like him, and that I should not sully this hand of mine by shampooing common men after having touched his delicate, graceful, exquisite person, I turned to the profession of gamblers to keep this accursed body and soul together.

(The courtesan looks at the maid with tears of joy.)

** MAID**тАФAnd then?

** SHAMPOOER**тАФThen one day, I lost ten pieces of gold to a man from whom I had won for several days.

** COURTESAN**тАФWell then?

** SHAMPOOER**тАФSo to-day as I happened by chance to come to this courtesan’s quarter, I was found; and through fear of him I entered this house. So now your ladyship knows everything.

** COURTESAN**тАФ(Aside) Oh pity! So I think do the birds wander about on the destruction of the sheltering tree.)(Aloud) Under these circumstances, you are one of us. My girl, come, send away that person.

** MAID**тАФVery well. (Exit)

** COURTESAN**тАФYou need not be anxious about the money. You may regard that the noble C─Бrudatta has paid it.

(Entering)

** MAID**тАФI have dismissed that person. He went away satisfied.

** SHAMPOOERтАФ**I am much obliged.

** COURTESAN**тАФYou may now leave and join your friends and feel happy.

** SHAMPOOERтАФ**I am disgusted with the world, and may even this very day renounce it. But, Madam, if I can impart this art to one of your attendants, I shall feel grateful to you.

** COURTESAN**тАФYou should rather wait upon the very person for whose sake you learnt the art.

** SHAMPOOER** тАФ(Aside) How cleverly has she declined my services! For who would spoil a good turn by accepting a return for it? (Aloud) good-bye, lady.

** COURTESAN**тАФYes, sir, good-bye, till we meet again.

** SHAMPOOER**тАФWell, as you say, lady. (Exit.)

** COURTESAN**тАФWell, methinks I hear a sound.

(Entering)

** ATTENDANT**тАФVicchittik─Б, Vicchittik─Б, where is my mistress?

** COURTESAN**тАФMy good girl, what is that?

** ATTENDANT**тАФOh, I feel cheated, that my mistress did not see Karс╣Зap┼лra’s exploit by just leaning forward through the casement, with bosom bowed.

** COURTESAN**тАФSmall men are easily elated. What makes you feel so conceited ?

** ATTENDANT**тАФMistress, listen :

As the auspicious elephant, Bhadrakapotaka, was returning at great speed from a bath, making the royal road fragrant with dripping ichor, he caught hold of an ascetic who was conspicuous by the red colour of his upper garment among a crowd of innumerable men in the street.

** COURTESAN**тАФWell, what happened next?

ATTENDANTтАФThen the ascetic was lashed by the strokes of his trunk, was hauled up between his tusks, and snatched by the feet with his trunk, so that the people started crying тАЬAlas, alas, he is torn to pieces, he is killedтАЭ; then I turned back the elephant with blows have of my fist and released the ascetic.

** COURTESAN**тАФOh, I feel so happy about it; well, what followed?

** ATTENDANT**тАФAnd then every one said, тАЬHow marvellous,this feat of the lad !тАЭ but nobody thought of rewarding me. Then, mistress, a certain noble youth glanced at those parts of his person where ornaments are usually worn, and felt with his fingers also, and finding nothing, he blamed his fate and sighed deeply; and then he sent me this mantle through an attendant saying that was all he had.

** COURTESAN**тАФWho can this be that imitates the virtues of the noble C─Бrudatta?

** MAID**тАФMistress, I am also curious to know that. Who could this one be ?

** COURTESAN**тАФIt must be some kindly gentleman.

** MAID**тАФWell, ask him.

** COURTESAN**тАФAh, dear, partiality for one man destroys all other qualities.

** MAID**тАФGood man, do you know his name?

** ATTENDANT**тАФNo, I don’t know.

** COURTESAN**тАФThat was very thoughtless ofyou.

** MAID**тАФIf so, of whom were you speaking now?

** ATTENDANT**тАФI know this much-he is good and without conceit.

** COURTESAN**тАФCome along, let us have a look at him.

** ATTENDANT**тАФLook,mistress, look. Here he goes.

** COURTESAN**тАФ(Looking from her mansion) My dear, he is the noble C─Бrudatta himself, with nothing but his sacred thread for upper garment. Before he goes a long way off, let us have a look at him.

(Exeunt Omnes)

End of the Second Act.

Act III

(Then enter the Hero and the Vid┼лс╣гaka.)

** HEROтАФ**Friend, a lute is indeed a jewel not sprung from the sea. For

Like a friend, it follows the lover’s heart; it is a discourse of flawless melody on the objects of his love; a beloved companion in the passionate delight of lovedalliance; a co-wife to ladies that comes between them and their loves. (1)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФIt is a long time, my friend, that the streets are deserted in response to proclamation. Even the dogs have gone to sleep. But we get no sleep. And here is moreover this other wonderful thing. I cannot enjoy this cursed lute. I wish it had its strings snapped in the stronger parts.

** HEROтАФ**Friend, the singing to-day was mostly sweet owing to a variety of emotional effects; and yet you did not enjoy it!

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФThat is exactly why I did not enjoy it. Even a sweet dish eaten in large quantities causes indigestion.

** HERO**тАФThe singing was in every way clear. For,

Passionate, loud and sweet, equable, clear, full of feeling, (although) not accompanied by gesturesтАФor what need to praise it highly in various ways by saying this and thatтАФif he were behind a wall, I should have thought it was a woman. (2)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФYou may praise as you like. But I have no respect for a man who sings and a woman who studies. A man singing does not look well like a priest wearing garlands of red flowers. And a woman studying, looks as ugly as a cow with a slit nose.

** HERO**тАФFriend, it is already mid-night. Darkness has settled in the streets, and the absence of any traffic makes Ujjayin─л appear to be hushed in sleep. For,

Having made room for darkness, the moon of the eighth day sets as, when a wild elephant plunges into water, the ends of his tusk are gradually sunk. (3)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФYou are quite right. Darkness gets its chancefrom the sinking moon and seems to descend from the house-top.

** HERO**тАФ(Stepping round) Here is our house. Vardham─Бnaka!Vardham─Бnaka !

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФVardham─Бnaka ! Vardham─Бnaka, open the door.

(Entering)

** SERVANT**тАФHo! the noble Maitreya !

** HERO**тАФVardham─Бnaka !

** SERVANTтАФ**Oh, my master! Sir, I salute you.

** HERO**тАФBring water to wash our feet.

** SERVANTтАФ**(Moving about) Here is water to wash the feet. (Washes the hero’s feet.)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФVardham─Бnaka, wash mine feet, too.

** SERVANT**тАФWhen the feet are well washed, you will be rolling on the ground. Waste water? Or rather bring (your

feet) I will wash (them). (Gesticulates the washing of Vid┼лс╣гaka’s feet.)

VID┼кс╣вAKAтАФO, the slave-boy has not only washed my feet but my face too.

HEROтАФFriend,

This sleep, that hangs upon the eyes, seems to creep over me from the region of the forehead, and swift ard invisible like old age it grows in intensity as it saps mortal’s strength. (4)

Maitreya, let us sleep.

(Exit servant.)

(Entering with a casket of jewellery in her hands)

A MAIDтАФNoble Maitreya, wake up, wake up.

VID┼кс╣вAKAтАФWhat is it, lady?

MAIDтАФI was to hand over this gold casket after the lapse of the sixth and seventh days. To-day is the eighth.

HEROтАФIs that Vasantasena’s property?

MAIDтАФYes. Tell him, master, tell him that he must take it.

HEROтАФTake it, Maitreya.

VID┼кс╣вAKAтАФWhy not take this jewellery inside the inner apartments?

HEROтАФIdiot! The mistress of the house must not see jewellery worn by outsiders.

VID┼кс╣вAKAтАФNo help! Bring it; I will take what is (sure) to be stolen by thieves.

(Maid gives it and exit.)

VID┼кс╣вAKAтАФNow, why did you give your mantle to the courtesan’s servant ?

HEROтАФOut of sympathy.

VID┼кс╣вAKAтАФWhat? Sympathy even for such a one ?

HEROтАФFriend, do not say so.

VID┼кс╣вAKAтАФI have to roll on the ground like an ass of burden.

** HERO**тАФI am troubled by sleep. Keep quiet.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФSleep well to rise a happy man. I, too, will sleep.

(Both sleep.)
(Then enter Sajjalaka.)

** SAJJALAKA**тАФHere I am.

By my strength and skill, I have made a passage for my work that would easily admit the breadth of my body. Now will I creep along the ground with my body rubbed like a snake that sheds his worn-out skin. (5)

Ha, I have entered here by cutting a hole at the sidedoor of the garden-wall. So now I will get into the inner square. (Reflecting in sadness) Oh,

Let wise men call it mean, this which goes on when folks are asleepтАФfor it is cruelty and not valour to overpower by deceit those that repose in trust.Yet this condemnable position which leaves a man independent of others, is far better than the folded hands of servility; and this was the course adopted by Drona’s son in days gone by when he slew the sleeping princes. (6)

(Reflecting)

I feel no compunction in my mind if I come across the house of a merchant who is rich and greedy, who disregards honest men, and is ruthless in his business. (7)

Let whatever happen! What will not the Love-God drive us to! Let me set to work. Oh! Which is the spot that has become loose by running water and can be broken through without a sound? Where can a gaping hole be cut into the wall which with ease can give a view of the interior? Where has the house become dilapidated, worn out with saltpetre and thinned by falling bricks? Where is it that I may not encounter women and (yet) gain my purpose? (8)

(Stepping round) Here is (revealed) the lay-out of the site. The presence of moisture shows this portion of the mansion to be the best (suited for my purpose) in the house. So here will I make a breach for entrance. Ha, but what kind of breach should I make now?

Lion-stride or full moon? Mouth of fish or crescent-moon? Tiger-jaw or triangle? Shall the breach look like a seat or like an elephant’s mouth? How can the votaries of my art be taken by surprise? (9)

Well, I will cut the тАШLion-strideтАЩ.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФOh, you are a wake, aren’t you?

** HERO**тАФWhat is it?

VID┼кс╣вAKAтАФI cannot sleep any more than a Buddhist mendicant who has made an assignation with a serving wench. My left eye throbs. I fancy I see a thief cutting a hole. If that is the feeling that wealth gives, I would belong to the tribe of the poor.

** HERO**тАФFie on you, you fool. You long for poverty !

** SAJJALAKA**тАФNow what shall I use to mark out the line of the breach? Why, this will do, sacred thread by day and measuring tape by night.

When to-night I shall have breached the walls of this (house), leaving them even after cutting, and applying the cutting instrument but once, the neighbours with gloomy faces will at dawn, tomorrow, condemn my crime but praise my skill. (10)

Bow to Kharapata. Bow to the Gods that go by night. (Does as decided on.) Well, well, I have finished my work. Let me now enter. (Entering) Ah, there is a lamp burning. I must move away. Tut! I am Sajjalaka; A cat to leap, a wolf to sneak away, a hawk to descry a house, sleep to gauge the strength of the slumbering, a snake to glide. Illusion itself in changing either form

or hue, goddess of speech to understand the dialects of the land, a light by night, darkness in dangers, the wind on land and a boat on water. (11)

(Looking around) Being a stranger, I have no knowledge of the extent of (this man’s) affluence; but I have entered relying on the appearance of the house. But I find no special piece of furniture. Is he a poor man after all? Or does he keep what is worth seeing concealed and hence out of use? But, the mansion is nobly built. He must be a man who has dissipated his fortune on pleasure.

Though so poor, yet out of love for his birth-place he keeps the house and dearly loves it, even when it is time to sell it. (12).

Well, let me see. Or rather I should not trouble a gentleman who is in the same plight as myself. I will go.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФOh, take this golden casket.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФDid he say тАШa golden casketтАЩ? Did he speak on seeing me? Or through want of courage he talks in sleep? Well. I must see. (Observing) He is really asleep. For

His breathing is free from fear, even, and comes at equal intervals; the body lies stretched out at the joints, extended beyond the measure of the bed. His eyes are firmly closed, the space between the eyelashes not quivering. Had he been feigning sleep, he would not have borne the lamp in his face. (13)

Now, where is it? Ah, it is revealed in the light of the lamp in a portion of the tattered mantle. He holds it firmly. This is a proper moment. Here I have some moths. I will release one to extinguish the lamp. (Releases one from a bee-box) Ha, he falls down after extinguishing the lamp.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФAlas! the lamp is out! I am robbed. Ho, C─Бrudatta, take this golden casket. I cannot sleep for fright any more than a trader who has lost the right road. I conjure thee, by my Brahminhood, if thou dost not take it.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФWhat need of imprecations? I will take it.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФ(Handing over) Now will I sleep undisturbed like a trader who has sold his merchandise.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФSleep sound, great Brahmin! (Reflecting) Ah! that I should take away what a Brahmin gives me in confidence !

A curse on poverty and on youth that knowsno remorse, for I blame this wicked act and yet do it.) (14)

(A drum is beaten behind the scenes.)

** SAJJALAKA**тАФ(Listening) Ah, it is morning. Well, I shall get away.

(Exit Sajjalaka.)

(Entering)

** MAID**тАФ(Shouting) Noble Maitreya, a thief cut a hole in the side-door of our orchard and entered.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**, (Rising in haste)тАФWhat say you, lady?

(The maid repeats тАЬIn the orchardтАФ.тАЭ etc.)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФCut a hole in the thief?

** MAID**тАФConfound the fool! A thief cut a hole and got in.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФWell, come, show it to me.

** MAID**тАФ(Stepping round) There.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФO damn! That son of a slave-girl, that cur got in all right. Lady, come, let us tell the glad news to C─Бrudatta.

(Both advancing)

Ho, C─Бrudatta, I have got some glad news for you.

** HERO**тАФ(Waking) What, glad news for me? Is Vasantasen─Б come?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФNot Vasantasen─Б, but Vasantasena is come.

** HERO**тАФRadanik─Б, what is it?

** MAID**тАФMaster, a thief has cut a hole in the side-door of our orchard and got in.

** HERO**тАФWhat, a thief got in ?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФWell, friend, you always say тАЬMaitreya is an idiot,тАЭ тАЬMaitreya is a blockhead.тАЭ Have I not acted wisely in handing that golden casket to you?

** HERO**тАФYou handed that to me?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФYes, of course.

** HERO**тАФWhat time?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФAt midnight.

** HERO**тАФWhat, at midnight? Did you really give me?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФYes, C─Бrudatta, I gave it to you when you wereawake.

** HERO**тАФAlas! The golden casket has been stolen.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФNow, give it back to me.

** HERO**тАФ(Aside)

Who will believe the truth? Everyone will suspect me. For in all crimes impotent poverty is an object of suspicion. (15)

(Entering)

** THE BRAHMIN LADY**тАФRadanik─Б, Radanik─Б, eome. She does not hear. Well I shall rap at the door. (Does so.)

** MAID**тАФOh, a rap at the door. My mistress calls me. (Moving about) Here I am, Mistress.

** LADY**тАФI hope they are not hurt or killed? My husband or the noble Maitreya ?

** MAID**тАФThey are all right, my master and the noble Maitreya. But the jewellery of that person is stolen by burglars.

** LADY**тАФStolen by burglars, you say?

** MAID**тАФYes.

** LADY**тАФHow is that person to be recompensed ?Well Iwill give this. (Touching her ears) Alas! This is only a palm leaf. How habit deceives me ! What may I do now? (Reflecting) Well, I have it. I have received from my family a necklace worth a lakh. But would my lord accept it, out of pride? Well, this is what I will do. (exit)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФWith bent head I beg your pardon for this fault which was caused by darkness. Now you may put it into my hands.

** HERO**тАФWhy do you worry me, now?

You have all these days known my character, and yet you do not believe me? How much more then that person that lives by her art and is clever at deceit? (16)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФSo, methinks, unfortunate as I am , I must have put it into the hands of the burglar. (Stands apart in dejection.)

** THE BRAHMIN LADY**тАФRadanik─Б, call the noble Maitreya.

** MAID**тАФNoble Maitreya, the mistress calls you.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФWhat, me?

** MAID**тАФYes, of course.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФWell, I will come. (Advances)

** LADY**тАФNoble Maitreya, please to accept this present.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФSuch a costly present ill goes with our condition. What is the occasion of this (present)?

** LADY**тАФWhy, I observe a fast on the sixth day : and the occasion for it is my desire to secure the blessings of a Brahmin by making him the present of the best of my possessions.
** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФBut to-day is the eighth day.

** LADY**тАФIt was through mistake that it was not performed. So to-day I offer worship.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФThe present is so out of proportion (to the occasion) that it seems to be made out of compassion. (Aside) What should I do, Radanik─Б ?

** MAID**тАФ(Aside) My mistress acts thus to free my master from debt by handing it to you, thinking that my master must be worried about what to give to that person. So accept it.

** LADY**тАФAs the pearl-stringтАЩ has sprung from water, and it is difficult to meet you, I have forgotten the formality. Take this.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФ(Taking) Let everything be. But there are tears in your eyes.

** LADY**тАФThe temple smoke has brought those tears to my eyes.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФI conjure thee by the noble C─Бrudatta, if you don’t tell the truth.

** LADY**тАФAlas! (Exit)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФShe has gone without speaking her grief in words but betraying it by her tears. (Advances) Ho, here it is.

** HERO**тАФWhat is it?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФThe fruit of marrying a lady from a family of equal rank.

** HERO**тАФSo my wife takes pity on me?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФYes, that is it.

** HERO**тАФFie on me. Today I feel a dead man.

So powerless I am through loss of wealth, that a woman pities me with her wealth. Thus the man is in fact but a woman, and the woman, man. (17)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA** тАФThe lady entreats you from her heart, I entreat you with my bowed head. Take this.

** HERO**тАФWell, as you say. (Taking) Friend, take this pearlstring and go to Vasantasen─Б.

My desire having indulged fully in my wealth now unworthily seeks woman’s wealth, hanging between

my pride and my duty. O fie, what good is a (noble) family if a man is poor? (18)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФOh that a necklace worth a lakh is to be given to recompense a golden casket worth but a trifle !

** HERO**тАФFriend, do not say so.
Give this as the price of that great confidence which inspired her to make the deposit with us. (19)

Exeunt Omnes
End of the Third Act.

ACT IV

(Enter Vasantasen─Б in love, and her maid with a pictureboard, holding a paint-box and brushes in her hand.)

** COURTESAN**тАФMy good girl, do you think it is like him?

** MAID**тАФMistress, that is exactly how that noble youth looked when I saw him from a distance with eyes that sought him with great regard in the hubbub of riot caused by the elephant.

** COURTESAN**тАФNow you speak falsely thus proving the proverb тАЬSly are those that live in courtesans’ quarterтАЭ.

** MAID**тАФWhat is that? Every one in courtesansтАЩ quarter is so politeтАЭ? Look you, my mistress, Nimba trees do grow in a Campaka garden. My heart is charmed that it is so very like. I am praising it in very truth: he is indeed, the very God of Love.

** COURTESAN**тАФMy good girl, I want to avoid being ridiculed by my friends.

** MAID**тАФThat is right. Courtesans, they say, regard their friends as their rivals.

(Enter another maid with ornaments in her hand.)

** MAID**тАФIS my mistress well?

** COURTESAN**тАФWell, my good girl, you are welcome.

** MAID**тАФMistress, mother bids :тАФ тАЬHere stands the lotus carriage brought into the gateway and turned round; so be quick with your ornaments and come along.тАЭ Here are the ornamentsтАФplease to put them on, mistress.

** COURTESAN**тАФWhat, does the noble C─Бrudatta honour me with those ornaments ?

** MAID**тАФNo, no; the person who sent these ornaments is the King’s brother-in-lawтАФSaс╣Гsth─Бna.

** COURTESAN**тАФGet thee gone, impudent creature !

** MAID**тАФForgive me, mistress, forgive me. I am simply repeating the message. (Falls at her feet.)

** COURTESAN**тАФRise, rise. I am impatient with the bad message, not with thee.
** MAID**тАФWhat should I tell mother?

** COURTESAN**тАФTell mammaтАФThat I will put on the ornamentswhen I shall have to go out to meet the noble C─Бrudatta.

** MAID**тАФVery well. (Exit.)

(Then enter Sajjalaka.)

** SAJJALAKA**тАФAt night I committed a condemnable wrong overcoming sleep and darkness and fear. But now at the rising of the Sun my courage gradully becomes fainter like the moon by day and I am filled with fear. (1)

Fortunately the day dawned after I had finished my work. Now I have done this just to redeem Madanik─БтАФVasantasen─Б’s servant-maid. (Stepping round) This isVasantasen─Б’s house.So I will enter. (Entering)Is Madanik─Б in the inner part of the house? But, courtesans are in the inner part during the early part of the day. So she must be just there. So I will call her. Madanik─Б! Madanik─Б!

** MAIDтАФ**(Listening) That sounds like Sajjalaka’s voice. Mistress is engaged. So I will advance (to him). (Advancing) Here I am.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФCome here, please.

** MAID**тАФWhy do you look so frightened?

** SAJJALAKA**тАФNot at all; but I want to tell you something.

** COURTESAN**тАФWell, my girl, put this picture-board on my bed. (Looking out) Where is the fool gone? Or rather she must not have gone far. So I will look for her. (Stepping round and looking) Oh, there she is, talking to some man whom she seems to be drinking up with her very loving eyes. I think this is some one who demands her of me by purchase.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФListen to a secret.

** COURTESAN**тАФIt is improper to listen to another’s secret; I will go away.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФWould Vasantasen─БтАФ(Stops when half through the words).

** COURTESAN**тАФI am the subject of their conversation. Well, I will listen. (Turns back again and waits.)

** SAJJALAKA**тАФGive you for a price?

** COURTESAN**тАФIt is the same person. Well, I will listen.

** MAID**тАФSajjalaka, mistress has already spoken of my giving away.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФWell then, give this to her; and tell her thus. These ornaments seem to be made to the measure of your body. Show them not openly but wear them for love of me. (2)

** MAID**тАФLet me have a look at them.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФTake. (Shows.)

** MAID**тАФIt seems I have already seen these ornaments.

** COURTESAN**тАФThese ornaments appear like mine.

** MAID**тАФTell me, tell me, how did you come by these?

** SAJJALAKA**тАФI acted daringly for love of you.

** BOTH**тАФOh, this rash fellow !

** MAID**тАФ(To herself) His form has become detestable to my mistress on account of this violent deed. (Aloud) Alas, for my sake you I have compromised both your person and character.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФIdiot, fortune dwells with daring.

** MAID**тАФYou are so ignorant. Who will sell his body for his life? Now in whose house did you perpetrate this breach of faith?

** SAJJALAKA**тАФAs I learnt in the morningтАФit was C─Бrudatta, the merchant’s son, who lives in the merchant’s square.

** BOTH**тАФHa!

** SAJJALAKA**тАФAll your limbs drooping in distress, eyes dilated in confusion, how you tremble like a doe pierced by shafts and (yet) are filled with compassion! (3)

** MAID**тАФTell the truth. In doing this violence in the merchant’s house, did you wound or kill with your weapon any noble youth?

** COURTESAN**тАФWell, she asks exactly as I should have asked.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФMadanik─Б, is this not enough that I should be adding another evil! Surely I have not wounded or killed any one with my weapon.

** MAID**тАФIs that true, Sajjalaka?

** SAJJALAKA**тАФYes.

** MAID**тАФThat is good, Sajjalaka. That pleases me.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФWhat pleases youтАФyou said? So, it is thus, Madanik─Б.

My heart being bound for love of you, I commit this crimeтАФ though sprung in a family of ancestors who lived content. How I preserve my passion-smitten frameтАФand you call me a friend and yet go to another ! (4)

** MAID**тАФSajjalaka, listen. These ornaments belong to my mistress. (Whispers in his ear). It is thus.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФSo, tortured by summer-heat and seeking shade, I have sought the self-same branch whose leaves erstwhile I stripped in ignorance. (5)

** COURTESAN**тАФSince he is repentingтАФI think he has committed a crime.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФMadanik─Б, what shall I do under the circumstances ?

** MAID**тАФReturn where they belong. My mistress will not put them on.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФBut if in anger he hands me over to the police as a thief, what shall I do then?

** MAID**тАФDon’t be afraid. He is a gentleman who will be pleased with good qualities.

** COURTESAN**тАФGood, dear girl, you are without reproach. How those words adorn you !

** SAJJALAKA**тАФBut I find it absolutely impossible to go there.

** MAID**тАФHere is another way.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФWhat is that other way?

** MAID**тАФDo the merchant’s son and my mistress recognise you?

** SAJJALAKA**тАФNot at all,

** MAID**тАФIn that case, give the jewellery to my mistress in the name of the merchant’s son. That done, you will be safe, that gentleman will be free from anxiety and I shall have nothing to worry about. Otherwise, were I to deceive my mistress I shall again be a slave.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФMadanik─Б, I am pleased.

** COURTESAN**тАФWell, I will retire to the inner room, and sit down. (Does so.)

** MAID**тАФCome, Sajjalaka, wait for me in the Love-God’s temple. I shall speak to my mistress at the proper moment.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФVery well. (Exit.)

(Then enter another maid.)

** MAID**тАФAll happiness to my Lady. Here comes a certain Brahmin from the merchant’s son to see my lady.

** COURTESAN**тАФ(Respectfully) Go, bring him quick.

** MAID**тАФVery well. (Advancing) Come, come, sir.

(Entering)

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФ(Looking all round) Ah, this splendour of the courtesan’s house! Here are learned men from various towns busy reading books. Various delicacies are under preparation. Lutes are played on. Gold-smiths are carefully designing various kinds of jewellery.

** MAIDтАФ**Here is my lady. Sir, please to advance.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФ(Approaching) Blessings to your ladyship.

** COURTESAN**тАФYou are welcome, sir. My dear, bring a seat for the gentleman, and water to wash his feet.

** MAID**тАФAs my lady commands. (Gives him a seat and water or his feet.) Please take this seat, sir.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФ(Sitting) Please sit down, lady. I have to say something.

** COURTESAN**тАФ(Sitting) I am all attention.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФWhat is the extent of the value of that jewellery?

** COURTESAN**тАФWhy do you ask me that, sir?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФListen, lady. You indeed deposited that jewellery with C─Бrudatta because you relied on his good qualities. But he has lost it in gambling.

** COURTESAN**тАФIn gambling? Well, that is right. What next?

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФPlease, therefore, to accept this pearl-necklace as price of the jewellery.

** COURTESAN**тАФ(To herself)тАФFie on this life of a courtesan! He despises me as a greedy woman. If I don’t accept it, it will be the same fault over again. (Aloud) Bring it, sir.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**тАФHere it is, take it, lady.

** COURTESAN** (Taking it)тАФTell him, sir, that I have accepted it.

** VID┼кс╣вAKA**. (To himself)тАФWell, she did not trouble to say a few formal words. (Aloud) Very well. (Gives and exit.)

** COURTESAN**тАФBravo, C─Бrudatta, bravo! How in this reverse of fortune you have saved your pride from a fall !

(Entering)

** MADANIK─А**тАФMistress, here comes a man from the merchant’s son and wants to see you.

** COURTESAN**тАФHave I seen him before, or is he a new comer?

** MADANIK─АтАФ**NO, mistress, I think he is some servant of that one.

** COURTESAN**тАФGo, bring him in.

** MADANIK─А**тАФ

Very well. (Exit)

** COURTESAN**тАФOh, what a lovely day!

(Then enter Madanik─Б with Sajjalaka.)

** SAJJALAKA**тАФHow painful is an uneasy conscienc!

If some one, walking briskly by, marks me,or if he quickly advances to me in confusion, or stands still, my mind suspects them all alike through its own guilt:for a man’s own guilt makes him suspicious.(6)

** MADANIK─А**тАФHere is my lady. Advance, sir.

** SAJJALAKA** (Advances)тАФAll happiness to your ladyship.

** COURTESAN**тАФWelcome, sir. My dear, give the gentlman a seat.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФLet be, let be. Here I take a seat. I have some business which must be speedily attended to.

** COURTESAN**тАФIf so, speak out, sir.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФI am sent by the noble C─Бrudatta with this message: тАФтАЬIt is difficult to take care of the jewellery entrusted to me because the house is in neglect through lack of use and the members of my family are away; so take it back.тАЭ

** COURTESAN**тАФWell, sir, give it to C─Бrudatta.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФLady, surely I shall not go (to him).

** COURTESAN**тАФI believe, you have brought this jewellery by committing theft at his house. You should have some consideration for his virtues, sir.

** SAJJALAKA**тАФ(To himself) How did she find me out?

** COURTESAN**тАФWho is there? Bring a carriage for the gentleman.

** MADANIK─А**тАФI seem to hear the sound of wheels; so the carriage must have come.

** COURTESAN**тАФ(Adorning Madanik─Б with her jewellery) Sir, get into the carriage with the lady.

** MADANIK─А**тАФWhat is this, mistress?

** COURTESAN**тАФNay, don’t say so. You are a free woman now. Take her, sir. (Taking hold of Madanik─Б, gives her over to Sajjalaka.)

** SAJJALAKA**тАФ (To himself) When can I requite her? Or rather, let evil be averted.

A man seeking to requite another, gains his wish (only) through (the latter’s) calamity. May that calamity of hers or of his befall their enemies. (7)

(Exit Sajjalaka with her.)

** COURTESAN**тАФCaturik─Б!

(Entering)

** A MAID**тАФHere I come, my lady.

** COURTESAN**тАФMy good girl, see, wide awake, I have seen a dream like this.

** MAID**тАФI am glad; that is just the play known as тАЬThe Ambrosial ActтАЭ.

** COURTESAN**тАФCome, we shall take this jewellery and go to the noble C─Бrudatta.

** MAID**тАФGood, my mistress. But, then, here is a storm come upтАФa friend to ladies going to their lovers.

** COURTESAN**тАФNow, wretch, don’t increase (my difficulties).

** MAID**тАФCome, mistress, come.

(Exeunt)

End of Act IV.

C─АRUDATTAM

NOTES

Act I

P. 1. The C─Бrudatta stands apart from the other plays of the group in this that its prologue is altogether different from that in the other plays and is unique in several ways. There is no benedictory stanzaтАФneither in the simple form nor in the form of the Mudr─Бlaс╣Гk─Бra wherein the names of the principal characters are woven together; the S┼лtradh─Бra speaks Pr─Бkс╣Ыta, which is unusual; the subject-matter of the prelude has nothing to do with the s┼лtradh─Бra’s proper business of staging a play; in fact he is not even conscious of the fact that he is there to introduce a play to the audience; and lastly the prologue, unlike the prologues in the other plays, is very lengthy.

I┬│. рдЬрд╛рд╡… рдЬрд╛рдгрд╛рдорд┐ тАФ the presenttense in the sense of the future рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдорд┐ according to тАЬрдпрд╛рд╡рддреН тАУ рдкреБрд░рд╛рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрдпреЛтАЭ рд░рд┐рддрд┐ рднрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ рд▓рдЯреН.

I. 18. рдХрд╛рдордВ рдкреНрд░рджреЛрд╖ etc. It is to be remembered that in the рдореГрдЪреНрдЫрдХ┬║ as soon as the Viс╣нa learns that Vasantasen─Б is in love with C─Бrudatta, his attitude towards her is changed. He becomes friendly to her and makes every effort to help her to escape from the clutches of the brutal ┼Ъak─Бra. Thus he makes the ┼Ъak─Бra repeat the words рд╡рд╛рдорддрдГ рддрд╕реНрдп ( рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрддрд╕реНрдп ) рдЧреГрд╣рдореН so as to give a hint to Vasantasen─Б to effect her escape into C─Бrudatta’s house, and also suggests to her by this stanza that although she is not to be seen owing to the darkness in the lane, yet she is being betrayed by the scent of her flowers and the jingle of her ornaments. All this sly cross-play of suggestion, however, is lost in the C─Бrudatta where the Viс╣нa still remains one of the tormenters of Vasantasen─Б.

II┬▓┬▓. рдмрд╣реБрдорд╛рдгреЛ рд╡рд┐рдЕ тАУ рдмрд╣реБрдорд╛рдирдГ is to be regarded as a рдмрд╣реБрд╡реНрд░реАрд╣рд┐ compoundтАФрдмрд╣реБрдГ рдорд╛рдирдГ рдпрд╕реНрдп рдпрдГтАФтАЬas lovely as he is respectable.тАЭ рдЕрддреНрдерд┐ рдЕрджрд┐рдмрд╣реБрдорджреЛ etc. What she means is тАЬLove requires and cherishes perfect confidence (рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд░рдореНрднрдГ). P. 25. IIтБ╡┬▓. рджреЗ рдорд╣реБрдЕрд░рд╛ рддреНрддрд┐ рдкреБрдЪреНрдЫреАрдЕрдиреНрддрд┐ ред тАУ рдкреБрдЪреНрдЫреАрдЕрдиреНрддрд┐ = рдкреГрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреЗтАФрдкрд░реНрдпрдиреБрдпреБрдЬреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдЙрдкрд╛рд▓рднреНрдпрдиреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН ред Woolner rendersтАЬ That is why they are called bees.тАЭ рдореГрдЪреНрдЫреж reads рд╡реБрдЪреНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐тАУ рдЙрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ редwhich makes a clear meaning. III. 1. рд╕рдВрдХреАрд░реНрдгрджреЛрд╖рд░рд╣рд┐рддрд╛… рдЧреЛрд╖реНрдареАтАФGaс╣Зapati explains this thus :тАФрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЗрд╖реБ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╕реЗрд╡рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпреЗрд╖реНрд╡рд░реНрдереЗрд╖реБ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рд╕рдВрдХреАрд░реНрдгрджреЛрд╖рд░рд╣рд┐рддрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЧрд╕рдЩреНрдХрд░рджреЛрд╖рд╢реВрдиреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реБрджреНрдзрдЧреАрддрд╛ рдЧреЛрд╖реНрдЯреА рдЧрд╛рдирд╕рджрдГред.Hence тАФ тАЬA discourse (рдЧреЛрд╖реНрдЯреА) of flawless melody on the objects of his love (рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп).тАЭ рдХреНрд░реАрдбрд╛рд░рд╕реЗрд╖реБ рдорджрдирд╡реНрдпрд╕рдиреЗрд╖реБтАФрдорджрдирд╡реНрдпрд╕рди is intense passion or love ; while рдХреНрд░реАрдбрд╛рд░рд╕ is to be taken as adjectival qualifying рдорджрдирд╡реНрдпрд╕рдиреЗрд╖реБ тАУ рдХреНрд░реАрдбрд╛рднрд┐рдГ (by dalliances) рд░рд╕рдГ рдпреЗрд╖реБ тАФ So that the expression means :тАФin the passionate delight of love-dalliances.

III. 18. This is not to be met with in theрдореГрдЪреНрдЫре░

Act IV

P. 47. IV┬╣┬│ рдкрд┐рдЪреБрдордиреНрджрд╛рдГтАУрдирд┐рдореНрдмрджреНрд░реБрдорд╛рдГред

** рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╣реНрдгреЗ**etc. This observation on the life and habits of courtesans is original with our author. It is not to be met with in the рдореГрдЪреНрдЫреж.

P. 48. IV. IтБ┤. **рддрдХреНрдХреЗрдорд┐… рдХреНрд╡рдПрдг рдордВ рдпрд╛рдЪреЗрджрд┐редтАФ**This is rather ambiguous. I have translated it thus :тАФтАЬThis is some one who demands her of me by purchase.тАЭ But in this I have taken рдорд╛рдВ as indirect object, and тАШherтАЩ as direct object although it is not there. What a plain and vulgar idea that would be, although our author seems to be capable of such impropriety ! In the рдореГрдЪреНрдЫреж we have :тАФрдПрд╕реЛ рд╕реЛ рдЬрдгреЛ рдПрджрдВ рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрджрд┐ рдЕрднреБрдЬрд┐рд╕реНрд╕рдВ рдХрд╛рджреБрдВ ред ( рдПрд╖рд╕ рдЬрдирдГ рдПрдирд╛рдВ рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдЕрднреБрдЬрд┐рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдВ рдХрд░реНрддреБрдореН ред).

P. 53. IV. 5тБ┤┬▓ рдЖрдЖрдорд┐рдПрд╣рд┐тАФрдЖрдЧрдорд┐рдХреИрдГтАФThis is explained by Woolner to mean ‘Visitors’. But the word means рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮреИрдГ.

IV. 55.рддрддреНрддрд╣реЛрджреЛ рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрддрд╕реНрдптАФIt should be remembered that in the previous act where the рд╡рд┐рджреВрд╖рдХ is asked by рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрдд

to go to рд╡рд╕рдиреНрддрд╕реЗрдирд╛ with the pearl-necklace no such message is given to him. In the рдореГрдЪреНрдЫ┬║, however, he is charged with the message in the III act and he delivers it when he sees her in act IV.

P. 57. IV. 6┬▓тБ╢. рдорд╛ рдЦреБ, рдорд╛ рдЦреБ… рдЕрдпреНрдпрд╛ рдЦреБ рд╕рд┐ рджрд╛рдгрд┐рдВ etc. Woolner curiously enough translates this thusтАФтАЬRestraining him with warning words you have now become his lawful wifeтАЭ. ** IV. 7. рдирд░рдГ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпреБрдкрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рд░реНрдереА** etc. The verse is not found in the рдореГрдЪреНрдЫ┬║. Woolner’s translation runs as follows:тАФтАЬThe man who looks for recompense does but gain calamity. May destruction fall on those that hate them, either him or the lady.тАЭ It seems that he has not rightly understood the drift of the passage. What Sajjalaka means is this :тАФ If he desired to requite Vasantasen─Б he could do so only when the latter suffered some calamity (рд╡рд┐рдкрддреНрддрд┐), so that to desire to requite her is to wish that some calamity should befall her. So rather than wish such a рд╡рд┐рдкрддреНрдХрд╛рд▓ to a friend and then seek to help him, why not wish that that рд╡рд┐рдкрддреНрдХрд╛рд▓ befell his or her enemies?

IV. 7тБ╖. рдЕрдореБрджрдВрдХрдгрд╛рдбрдЕрдВтАУрдЕрдореГрддрд╛рдЩреНрдХрдирд╛рдЯрдХрдореН тАУ We have in рдкрджреНрдордкреНрд░рд╛рднреГрддрдХрдВ, a рднрд╛рдг attributed to рд╢реВрджреНрд░рдХ, a similar remark рд╕рд╛рдзреБ рднреЛрдГ рдЕрдореГрддрдЩреНрдХреЛ ( рдЕрдореГрддрд╛рдЩреНрдХ ? ) рдирд╛рдЯрдХрд╛рдЩреНрдХрдГ рд╕рдВрд╡реГрддреНрддрдГ ред; to my mind the whole conversation here seems to give finality to the play and that the remark in the colophon рдЕрд╡рд╕рд┐рддрдВ рдЪрд╛рд░реБрджрддреНрддрдореН is well justified. There is no рднрд░рддрд╡рд╛рдХреНрдп at the end.
